        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer110121578" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6542199362955464905">This is an excellent collection, with the titled novella being my favorite and having some truly wonderful prose throughout. It struck me as a southern tall tale crossed with that terrible "love gone wrong" plus Southern Gothic. So many parts equal a glorious whole for the reader if not for Miss Amelia.The descriptions of the café and the changes wrought on the town and its inhabitants are exciting to read, so full of life.<br/><br/><br/> <i>But the pride that the café brought to this town had an<br/> effect on almost</i></span>
  <span id="freeText6542199362955464905" style="display:none">This is an excellent collection, with the titled novella being my favorite and having some truly wonderful prose throughout. It struck me as a southern tall tale crossed with that terrible "love gone wrong" plus Southern Gothic. So many parts equal a glorious whole for the reader if not for Miss Amelia.The descriptions of the café and the changes wrought on the town and its inhabitants are exciting to read, so full of life.<br /><br /><br /> <i>But the pride that the café brought to this town had an<br /> effect on almost everyone, even the children. For in order to<br /> come to the café you did not have to buy the dinner, or a <br /> portion of liquor. There were cold bottled drinks for a nickel.<br /> And if you could not even afford that, Miss Amelia had a drink<br /> called Cherry Juice which sold for a penny a glass, and was<br /> pink-colored and very sweet. Almost everyone, with the exception<br /> of Reverend T. M. Willin, came to the café at least once during<br /> the week. Children love to sleep in houses other than their<br /> own, and to eat at a neighbor's table; on such occasions they<br /> behave themselves decently and are proud. The people in the town <br /> were likewise proud when sitting at the tables in the café.<br /> They washed before coming to Miss Amelia's, and scraped their<br /> feet very politely on the threshold as they entered the café.<br /> There, for a few hours at least, the deep bitter knowing that<br /> you are not worth much in this world could be laid low.</i><br /> (p 54)<br /><br /><br />But of course this is more than the tale of a town and a café and Miss Amelia. It's also the tale of the hunchback dwarf, Cousin Lymon, and the one Marvin Macy. If you are not familiar with them, you must read the story!<br /><br />Of the other stories included in tis collection, my favorites are "Wunderkind" and "The Sojourner". Heartsick lovers and outsiders people her stories and seem to be searching for other places and people. But the star is "The Ballad of the Sad Café", so come and stay a while and meet these country folk.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6542199362955464905" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_871248755" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/871248755" />
    <a title="Connie G" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5364077-connie-g"><img alt="Connie G" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1307502493p2/5364077.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/871248755?book_show_action=true">Mar 03, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Connie G" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Connie G" href="/user/show/5364077-connie-g">Connie G</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5364077-connie-g?shelf=southern-lit">southern-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5364077-connie-g?shelf=short-stories">short-stories</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5364077-connie-g?shelf=classic">classic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5364077-connie-g?shelf=georgia">georgia</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer871248755" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14456774999417414065">Note: Spoilers Ahead<br/><br/>The novella "The Ballad of the Sad Cafe" is a Southern Gothic work with eccentric, lonely characters in a rundown Georgia town. Miss Amelia Evans is a six foot two inch rugged woman. She's the owner of a general store, and does a bit of healing with herbs on the side to help the townspeople. They gossip about her ten day marriage to Marvin Macy which ended after she refused his sexual advances. Marvin left town for a life of crime, and landed in the penitentiary.<br/><br/>A hunchback d</span>
  <span id="freeText14456774999417414065" style="display:none">Note: Spoilers Ahead<br /><br />The novella "The Ballad of the Sad Cafe" is a Southern Gothic work with eccentric, lonely characters in a rundown Georgia town. Miss Amelia Evans is a six foot two inch rugged woman. She's the owner of a general store, and does a bit of healing with herbs on the side to help the townspeople. They gossip about her ten day marriage to Marvin Macy which ended after she refused his sexual advances. Marvin left town for a life of crime, and landed in the penitentiary.<br /><br />A hunchback dwarf, Lymon Willis, comes to the store professing to be Miss Amelia's cousin. Miss Amelia takes him in, and they turn the store into a bright cafe where the townspeople socialize. Although Lymon seems to be a parasite, Miss Amelia loves him and seems happy living with him. When Marvin gets out of jail, Lymon is fascinated by him and ignores Miss Amelia. A triangular love relationship is formed where the beloved does not love the person who loves them. <br /><br />Carson McCullers had a troubled marriage with her spouse who had a male lover. She would certainly understand the dynamics of a triangular relationship, and the devastation that could result. There are a wonderful pages in the book, too long to quote here, about the relationship between the beloved and the loved.<br /><br />The book also contained six short stories about love:<br /><br />"Wunderkind" is about a promising young pianist who loses her emotional feel for the music. (McCullers had taken piano lessons for years before giving it up when her piano teacher moved when her husband had a job relocation.)<br /><br />"The Jockey" focuses on the emotions felt by an older jockey when he sees the indifference of a group of businessmen to the news that his friend, a younger jockey, has a permanent injury. The businessmen are only concerned about money and winning, not personal tragedy.<br /><br />"Madame Zelensky and the King of Poland" is about a musician who tells exaggerated stories. Her real life has no time for anything but the music she loves, so she invents a personal life.<br /><br />"The Sojourner" tells about a man who sees his ex-wife and her new happy family. He realizes he needs a life with deeper meaning.<br /><br />"A Domestic Dilemma" involves a husband coming home from work to find his wife drunk again, and the children unattended. How much will his young, beloved children remember about her behavior, and can their marriage last? McCullers writes about the "immense complexity of love" in this story.<br /><br />"A Tree, A Rock, A Cloud" shows a drunk man telling a paperboy about the science of love. After losing the love of a woman, he decided to start loving again on a small scale, loving a tree, a rock, a cloud. A sad story.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14456774999417414065" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2401550369" />
    <a title="Josh" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6041973-josh"><img alt="Josh" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598551141p2/6041973.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2401550369?book_show_action=true">May 25, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Josh" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Josh" href="/user/show/6041973-josh">Josh</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6041973-josh?shelf=2018">2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2401550369" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13496150360302165012"><b>(3.5)</b> While reading McCullers, you feel an underlying sadness towards her characters. Whether it be their heartache and trying to find ways to cope with what life has given them or their random birth into a low class of society that has kept them in a state of ignorant bliss, you find that the characters speak to the reader, but not in an overwhelming way. That underlying sadness is sometimes so subtle that it doesn't quite make me feel as much as many others sad prose, hence why my rating isn't</span>
  <span id="freeText13496150360302165012" style="display:none"><b>(3.5)</b> While reading McCullers, you feel an underlying sadness towards her characters. Whether it be their heartache and trying to find ways to cope with what life has given them or their random birth into a low class of society that has kept them in a state of ignorant bliss, you find that the characters speak to the reader, but not in an overwhelming way. That underlying sadness is sometimes so subtle that it doesn't quite make me feel as much as many others sad prose, hence why my rating isn't higher.<br /><br />Don't get me wrong, her writing is top notch; put her side by side with many authors in the last 100 years and she'd probably be in the upper echelon of the category.<br /><br />All of these stories are generally good, but I'd recommend <i>Wunderkind</i>, <i>The Sojourner</i> and <i>A Domestic Dilemma</i> (my favorite) as the top 3 in this collection. The novella which the book is named for is nice, but could've easily been shortened for maximum effect.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_2306833348" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2306833348" />
    <a title="Lotte" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25309949-lotte"><img alt="Lotte" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1408555448p2/25309949.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2306833348?book_show_action=true">Apr 03, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lotte" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lotte" href="/user/show/25309949-lotte">Lotte</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title=" " href="/book/show/42400707-the-ballad-of-the-sad-caf-and-other-stories">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25309949-lotte?shelf=a-classics">a-classics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25309949-lotte?shelf=c-20th-century">c-20th-century</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25309949-lotte?shelf=a-short-fiction">a-short-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25309949-lotte?shelf=2020-read">2020-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25309949-lotte?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2306833348" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4257943116509670533">The sensation of loneliness threads through Carson McCullers' short stories. It's fairly easy to associate McCullers' work with loneliness as it's literally in the title of her most famous novel, but I do think you're more than justified in doing so. The melancholia and longing entwined with loneliness permeate everything she writes about. Moments of alienation can be found in all of the stories in this collection — whether she writes about Miss Amelia, the enigmatic owner of the sad café, a hus</span>
  <span id="freeText4257943116509670533" style="display:none">The sensation of loneliness threads through Carson McCullers' short stories. It's fairly easy to associate McCullers' work with loneliness as it's literally in the title of her most famous novel, but I do think you're more than justified in doing so. The melancholia and longing entwined with loneliness permeate everything she writes about. Moments of alienation can be found in all of the stories in this collection — whether she writes about Miss Amelia, the enigmatic owner of the sad café, a husband coming home to his alcoholic wife or a teenage pianist, a "wunderkind" yearning for recognition. She perfectly dissects how the urge to connect with one another can go awry, which makes her stories feel very <i>human</i> somehow, very empathetic and moving. I can't wait to read more by her!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4257943116509670533" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8665262-the-ballad-of-the-sad-caf-and-other-stories">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21106693-sherril?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21106693-sherril?shelf=kindle">kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21106693-sherril?shelf=literary-fiction">literary-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21106693-sherril?shelf=short-stories">short-stories</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1522809726" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer353903001317810438"><strong>Stories by Carson McCullers, reason enough to read them. </strong><br/><br/>I started reading Ballad of the Sad Cafe and Other Stories for two reasons. 1. Carson McCullers had authored them and she had written two of my all time favorite books, The Member of the Wedding (read recently) and The Heart is a Lonely Hunter (read in high school). 2. Though I prefer novels to short stories, I couldn't pass up a book with the title, The Ballad of the Sad Cafe. <br/><br/>These stories were definitely more revealing of the author's q</span>
  <span id="freeText353903001317810438" style="display:none"><strong>Stories by Carson McCullers, reason enough to read them. </strong><br /><br />I started reading Ballad of the Sad Cafe and Other Stories for two reasons. 1. Carson McCullers had authored them and she had written two of my all time favorite books, The Member of the Wedding (read recently) and The Heart is a Lonely Hunter (read in high school). 2. Though I prefer novels to short stories, I couldn't pass up a book with the title, The Ballad of the Sad Cafe. <br /><br />These stories were definitely more revealing of the author's quirkiness than were my two much loved novels. Quirkiness aside, I could read Carson McCullers for her language alone. From the story from which the book gets its name - "It was toward midnight on the soft quiet evening in April. The sky was the color of blue swamp Iris, the moon clear and bright".<br />"Down by the creek the square brick factory was yellow with light". "His face was both soft and sassy". "It was not a common thing to have an unknown hunchback walk to the store at midnight and then sit down and cry". --why, I'd sleep like I was drowned in warm axle grease". "Stumpy MacPhail". These were just some of the characters in Miss Amelia's liquor filled Sad Cafe. There were only "3 good people" and "The room was still as death". This story and most of the others put me in mind of O Henry's stories in their artful turn of phrases, unique language and quirkiness of characters and circumstances. <br /><br />There is humor, drama, ridiculousness, an "interior life that is insufficient without the artifice of alcohol" and an absurd little tale about a callous cafe owner, a man who may or may not be crazy who tells a young boy wearing an aviator type helmet that he loves him. <br /><br />Like most of McCullers stories, they are about loneliness and love and love loss. However, none of the stories hold a candle to the novels, The Heart is a Lonely Hunter or my favorite, The Member of the Wedding, but they are written by Carson McCullers, reason enough to read them.</span>
  <a data-text-id="353903001317810438" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18795193-stefania?shelf=cuentos-y-relatos">cuentos-y-relatos</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2409208658" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12883612283524115657">Beautiful, beautiful book. This was my second approach to McCullers's work, and I can say, beyond a shadow of a doubt, that I've become one of her admirers. <br/><br/>I'm the kind of reader that tends to put the characters and the <i>human element</i> above the story line and everything else, so I'm always amazed by authors who <i>get it</i>, and it's obvious that McCullers is one of them. She understands loneliness. She understands love. She understands pain. And that, the deep comprehension of people's feelings and b</span>
  <span id="freeText12883612283524115657" style="display:none">Beautiful, beautiful book. This was my second approach to McCullers's work, and I can say, beyond a shadow of a doubt, that I've become one of her admirers. <br /><br />I'm the kind of reader that tends to put the characters and the <i>human element</i> above the story line and everything else, so I'm always amazed by authors who <i>get it</i>, and it's obvious that McCullers is one of them. She understands loneliness. She understands love. She understands pain. And that, the deep comprehension of people's feelings and behaviors is what makes her, in my opinion, one of the great writers of the past century.<br /><br />***<br /><br />Hermoso, hermoso libro. Esta fue mi segunda aproximación a la obra de McCullers y puedo decir, sin duda alguna, que me he convertido en una de sus admiradoras.<br /><br />Pertenezco a ese tipo de lectores que tiende a poner los personajes y el <i>elemento humano</i> por sobre la historia y todo lo demás, por lo que siempre me sorprenden los autores que <i>lo entienden</i>, y es obvio que McCullers es una de ellos. Ella entiende la soledad. Entiende el amor. Entiende el dolor. Y eso, esa profunda comprensión de los sentimientos y comportamientos de las personas, es lo que la convierte, en mi opinión, en una de las grandes escritoras del siglo pasado.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12883612283524115657" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14864161075767107614">"Leo had run a night cafe for 14 years, and he held himself to be a critic of craziness." That line is from the last story in the book, "A Tree, A Rock, A Cloud". I wish I knew how an author can come up with a sentence that says so much in 19 words. That's my favorite sentence but by no means the only perfect one in this collection. And as for the title story, it's just brilliant and awesome. Miss Amelia will stay a part of my psyche for a long time.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer17228826445345497036">Carson McCullers was obviously a talented writer, and while I didn't <i>love</i> "The Ballad of Sad Cafe" with a capital "L"(personal preference kind of thing), I did enjoy the other short stories included.<br/><br/>Recommend this to those who appreciate the "literary" genre. I haven't read a lot of Eudora Welty's work, but "The Ballad of Sad Cafe" reminded me of the one novella I did read by Welty, <i>The Robber Bridegroom</i>, in terms of story telling and overall quality of writing.</span>

<div id="review_3244787673" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3244787673" />
    <a title="Andy Weston" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/313206-andy-weston"><img alt="Andy Weston" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1190073185p2/313206.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3244787673?book_show_action=true">Mar 27, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andy Weston" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andy Weston" href="/user/show/313206-andy-weston">Andy Weston</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/313206-andy-weston?shelf=southern-gothic">southern-gothic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/313206-andy-weston?shelf=short-stories">short-stories</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/313206-andy-weston?shelf=novella">novella</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3244787673" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3454295900096645842">Populated by three eccentric characters, McCullers's classic novella is to do with loneliness, and looking for love, and finding it in the most unlikely places. The setting is a dreary town, down on its luck, with boarded up houses and a boarded up cafe, that is still reeling from the after effects of a strange love triangle. <br/>Its a splendidly told comic tragedy that ponders whether being in a unsatisfactory and often painful relationship is preferable to living alone..<br/><blockquote>Once you have lived with an</blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText3454295900096645842" style="display:none">Populated by three eccentric characters, McCullers's classic novella is to do with loneliness, and looking for love, and finding it in the most unlikely places. The setting is a dreary town, down on its luck, with boarded up houses and a boarded up cafe, that is still reeling from the after effects of a strange love triangle. <br />Its a splendidly told comic tragedy that ponders whether being in a unsatisfactory and often painful relationship is preferable to living alone..<br /><blockquote>Once you have lived with another, it is a great torture to have to live alone. The silence of a firelit room when suddenly the clock stops ticking, the nervous shadows in an empty house — it is better to take in your mortal enemy than face the terror of living alone.</blockquote><br /><br />I read the version that contained 6 other very short stories, each of only about 6 to 8 pages. These reminded me of walking down a street and looking into windows, small glimpses of people's lives. <br />The last one, <i>A Tree, A Rock, A Cloud</i>, sticks in my mind the most - a cafe with some older guys drinking in it, a young paper boy drops in, and one of the guys tries to explain to the boy the meaning of love.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3454295900096645842" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('+znkFW7C/c1OSrZMOSeuRem3X+bwmlfiOz2GrY9JFt/QaVfKMJWDXgPIqlGMWBPnBlCNI/0rhRzQchSdGEiaLg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('5+LRYxrM1uMtxoTctkfvh1X7R3+fTQM4RYwOrJHctEnMsmK8RJuocGBEmMEDOFIluhyVupL80cauw5ycBt04uA==')})
  }

the Outcast Indian Maiden,&quot; are the first great works of a great American writer.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"7964285380464848132\" href=\"#\" onclick=\"swapContent(\$(this));; return Just who are these green women? They are powerful (one was NDiaye’s disciplinarian grade-school teacher). They are mysterious (one haunts a house like a ghost and may be visible only to the author). They are seductive (one stole a friend’s husband). And they are unbearably personal (one is NDiaye’s own mother). They are all, in their way, aspects of their creator, at once frightening, menacing, and revealing of everything submerged within the consciousness of this singular literary talent. A courageous, strikingly honest, and unabashedly innovative self-portrait, NDiaye’s kaleidoscopic look at the women in green is a revelation to us all — about how we form our identities, how we       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/3506.Carson_McCullers">About Carson McCullers</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/3506.Carson_McCullers"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1335451237p3/3506.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/3506.Carson_McCullers">Carson McCullers
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
1,977
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer14077687327449178243">Carson McCullers was an American who wrote fiction, often described as Southern Gothic, that explores the spiritual isolation of misfits and outcasts of the South. <br/><br/>From 1935 to 1937 she divided her time, as her studies and health dictated, between Columbus and New York and in September 1937 she married an ex-soldier and aspiring writer, Reeves McCullers. They began their married life in Charlotte,</span>
  <span id="freeText14077687327449178243" style="display:none">Carson McCullers was an American who wrote fiction, often described as Southern Gothic, that explores the spiritual isolation of misfits and outcasts of the South. <br /><br />From 1935 to 1937 she divided her time, as her studies and health dictated, between Columbus and New York and in September 1937 she married an ex-soldier and aspiring writer, Reeves McCullers. They began their married life in Charlotte, North Carolina where Reeves had found some work. There, and in Fayetteville, North Carolina, she wrote her first novel, <i>The Heart Is a Lonely Hunter</i>, in the Southern Gothic tradition. <br /><br />The title, suggested by McCullers's editor, was taken from Fiona MacLeod's poem "The Lonely Hunter." However, many (including Carson McCullers) claim she wrote in the style of Southern Realism, a genre inspired by Russian Realism. The novel itself was interpreted as an anti-fascist book. Altogether she published eight books. <br /><br /><i>The Heart Is a Lonely Hunter</i> (1940), written at the age of twenty-three, <i>Reflections in a Golden Eye</i> (1941), and <i>The Member of the Wedding</i> (1946), are the best-known. The novella <i>The Ballad of the Sad Cafe</i> (1951) also depicts loneliness and the pain of unrequited love. She was an alumna of Yaddo in Saratoga, New York.<br /><br /><i>The Heart Is a Lonely Hunter</i> was filmed in 1968 with Alan Arkin in the lead role. <i>Reflections in a Golden Eye</i> was directed by John Huston (1967), starring Marlon Brando and Elizabeth Taylor. Some of the film was shot in New York City and on Long Island, where Huston was permitted to use an abandoned Army installation. <br /><br />Many of the interiors and some of the exteriors were done in Italy. "I first met Carson McCullers during the war when I was visiting Paulette Goddard and Burgess Meredith in upstate New York," said Huston in <i>An Open Book</i> (1980). <br /><br />"Carson lived nearby, and one day when Buzz and I were out for a walk she hailed us from her doorway. She was then in her early twenties, and had already suffered the first of a series of strokes. I remember her as a fragile thing with great shining eyes, and a tremor in her hand as she placed it in mine. It wasn't palsy, rather a quiver of animal timidity. But there was nothing timid or frail about the manner in which Carson McCullers faced life. And as her afflictions multiplied, she only grew stronger."<br /><br />After lifelong health problems including severe alcoholism, McCullers died of brain hemorrhage. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14077687327449178243" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>

<div class="clear"></div></div></div><div class="bigBoxBottom"></div></div>

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/952665-the-ballad-of-the-sad-caf">Quotes from The Ballad of the...</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;First of all, love is a joint experience between two persons — but the fact that it is a joint experience does not mean that it is a similar experience to the two people involved. There are the lover and the beloved, but these two come from different countries. Often the beloved is only a stimulus for all the stored-up love which had lain quiet within the lover for a long time hitherto. And somehow every lover knows this. He feels in his soul that his love is a solitary thing. He comes to know a new, strange loneliness and it is this knowledge which makes him suffer. So there is only one thing for the lover to do. He must house his love within himself as best he can; he must create for himself a whole new inward world — a world intense and strange, complete in himself. Let it be added here that this lover about whom we speak need not necessarily be a young man saving for a wedding ring — this lover can be man, woman, child, or indeed any human creature on this earth.<br /><br />Now, the beloved can also be of any description. The most outlandish people can be the stimulus for love. A man may be a doddering great-grandfather and still love only a strange girl he saw in the streets of Cheehaw one afternoon two decades past. The preacher may love a fallen woman. The beloved may be treacherous, greasy-headed, and given to evil habits. Yes, and the lover may see this as clearly as anyone else — but that does not affect the evolution of his love one whit. A most mediocre person can be the object of a love which is wild, extravagant, and beautiful as the poison lilies of the swamp. A good man may be the stimulus for a love both violent and debased, or a jabbering madman may bring about in the soul of someone a tender and simple idyll. Therefore, the value and quality of any love is determined solely by the lover himself.<br /><br />It is for this reason that most of us would rather love than be loved. Almost everyone wants to be the lover. And the curt truth is that, in a deep secret way, the state of being beloved is intolerable to many. The beloved fears and hates the lover, and with the best of reasons. For the lover is forever trying to strip bare his beloved. The lover craves any possible relation with the beloved, even if this experience can cause him only pain.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/30407-first-of-all-love-is-a-joint-experience-between-two">1107 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;But the hearts of small children are delicate organs. A cruel beginning in this world can twist them into curious shapes. The heart of a hurt child can shrink so that forever afterward it is hard and pitted as the seed of a peach. Or again, the heart of such a child may fester and swell until it is a misery to carry within the body, easily chafed and hurt by the most ordinary things.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/249748-but-the-hearts-of-small-children-are-delicate-organs-a">175 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
        <a class="actionLink" style="float: right" href="/work/quotes/952665-the-ballad-of-the-sad-caf">More quotes&hellip;</a>
